      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16689563735511902942">It began with Benny Hogan and Eve Malone, growing up, inseparable, in the village of Knockglen. Benny—the only child, yearning to break free from her adoring parents...Eve—the orphaned offspring of a convent handyman and a rebellious blueblood, abandoned by her mother's wealthy family to be raised by nuns. Eve and Benny—they knew the sins and secrets behind every villager'</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16689563735511902942">It began with Benny Hogan and Eve Malone, growing up, inseparable, in the village of Knockglen. Benny—the only child, yearning to break free from her adoring parents...Eve—the orphaned offspring of a convent handyman and a rebellious blueblood, abandoned by her mother's wealthy family to be raised by nuns. Eve and Benny—they knew the sins and secrets behind every villager's lace curtains...except their own.<br /><br /> It widened at Dublin, at the university where Benny and Eve met beautiful Nan Mahlon and Jack Foley, a doctor's handsome son. But heartbreak and betrayal would bring the worlds of Knockglen and Dublin into explosive collision. Long-hidden lies would emerge to test the meaning of love and the strength of ties held within the fragile gold bands of a...<strong>Circle Of Friends. </strong></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_5047092">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5047092" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/37088-holly" class="left imgcol" title="Holly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1182606190p2/37088.jpg" alt="Holly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/5047092?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 24, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/37088-holly" class="user" title="Holly">Holly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/41977.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099498599" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/37088-holly?shelf=socalled-chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">socalled-chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/37088-holly?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5047092">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4280716204729056461">I confess to loving what we at the bookstore used to consider "old lady novels." You know, written by nice old ladies, and featuring stock characters such as "Comfortable old lady who smells like violets," "Troubled young boy who will probably run away, thus becoming the catalyst to resolve the troubles of his father, who is..." "Bitter middle aged widower who just needs a little lovin'," and "Beautiful woman who provides said lovin'."<br /><br />Well, I've moved on from Rosamunde Pilcher, though The Shell</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4280716204729056461">I confess to loving what we at the bookstore used to consider "old lady novels." You know, written by nice old ladies, and featuring stock characters such as "Comfortable old lady who smells like violets," "Troubled young boy who will probably run away, thus becoming the catalyst to resolve the troubles of his father, who is..." "Bitter middle aged widower who just needs a little lovin'," and "Beautiful woman who provides said lovin'."<br /><br />Well, I've moved on from Rosamunde Pilcher, though The Shell Seekers will always hold a place in my heart. <br /><br />But two summers ago when we moved here and stayed with the in-laws for a time, I had a chance to read every single book ever written by Maeve Binchy. My husband mocked, while I only craved bon bons.<br /><br />Sure, she writes old lady novels. But her characters are distinct and fully-formed. There is a lot of conflict because they are almost always Catholic. There is some strong criticism of the Church and the rifts it causes in a woman's life as she tries to reconcile her faith/upbringing with the urges of her body. Some of her plots are simplistic, but the emotions never are.<br /><br />Note: I met her when she spoke at a women's lit class when I was in college. Circle of Friend was just coming out as a movie, and she was very excited. She's a sweet lady and very funny.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4280716204729056461">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/3103000-tea-jovanovi" class="left imgcol" title="Tea Jovanovi?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442608110p2/3103000.jpg" alt="Tea Jovanovi?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/604634954?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 01, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3103000-tea-jovanovi" class="user" title="Tea Jovanovi?">Tea Jovanovi?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17876891-krug-prijatelja" title="Hardcover 9788679280282" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3103000-tea-jovanovi?shelf=editor-of-serbian-edition" class="actionLinkLite">editor-of-serbian-edition</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3103000-tea-jovanovi?shelf=books-i-ve-sold-as-scout" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-ve-sold-as-scout</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3103000-tea-jovanovi?shelf=translated-it" class="actionLinkLite">translated-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer604634954">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13626452718158728057">Nažalost, Mev je prošlog leta preminula i ostali smo bez najtoplije irske autorke... Njene knjige plene toplinom i pri?ama o obi?nim ljudima i njihovim sudbinama... Knjige za one od 12-100 godina... <br /><br />Ovo je pri?a o dve devoj?ice iz male varošice u Irskoj i njihovom odrastanju... Veoma uspešno je i ekranizovana... A moram da se pohvalim da sam tokom prevoda pronašla dve materijalne greške u originalu i da sam prva posle 35 izdanja koja je ta knjiga imala na engleskom i posle svih engleskih urednik</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13626452718158728057">Nažalost, Mev je prošlog leta preminula i ostali smo bez najtoplije irske autorke... Njene knjige plene toplinom i pri?ama o obi?nim ljudima i njihovim sudbinama... Knjige za one od 12-100 godina... <br /><br />Ovo je pri?a o dve devoj?ice iz male varošice u Irskoj i njihovom odrastanju... Veoma uspešno je i ekranizovana... A moram da se pohvalim da sam tokom prevoda pronašla dve materijalne greške u originalu i da sam prva posle 35 izdanja koja je ta knjiga imala na engleskom i posle svih engleskih urednika koji su to ?itali i dopravljali, i posle bezbrojnih prevoda na razne jezike, koje je ta knjiga imala... Njena agentkinja je bila bez teksta... :) E pa, i to se dešava, da autori prave materijalne greške, a prevodioci to isprave... Ne ?esto, ali dešava se... :)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13626452718158728057">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15330153324645991519">Still one of my favourite books. Best written book ever. Okey, I love Maeve Binchy, but this book is smashing. I love it from the first until the last page.<br />You'll love all the characters, especially the friendship between Benny and Eve. And eventhough you loathes Nan's behavior, somehow you'll understand her. You'll fall in love very quickly at Jack Folley, and as soon as that you'll find yourself annoyed by his taken-for-granted-act- to our lovable Benny.<br />As other's Maeve writing, it's all detai</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15330153324645991519">Still one of my favourite books. Best written book ever. Okey, I love Maeve Binchy, but this book is smashing. I love it from the first until the last page.<br />You'll love all the characters, especially the friendship between Benny and Eve. And eventhough you loathes Nan's behavior, somehow you'll understand her. You'll fall in love very quickly at Jack Folley, and as soon as that you'll find yourself annoyed by his taken-for-granted-act- to our lovable Benny.<br />As other's Maeve writing, it's all details that we feel we really in their circle of friends in Ireland.<br />I love the part when Eve said to Benny "Someday I'll push down someone for you," after Benny 'rescued' her from a nasty-mouth girl who made fun of her. That's the real beginning of their beautiful friendship.<br />Everytime I read this book (yes, I read it more than twice), it always remind me of how valuable friendship is, and how blessed are the people who has true friends. (thanks my angels)<br />I also love the last two pages, especially the part when Benny looked up the sky, and all she saw was the smoke in the night sky, and she knew that Jack's face is among the friends, not taking the whole night sky.<br />That sentence really describe a great closure about Benny's feeling for Jack. Benny finally let him go, eventhough Jack still loves her the same (even more, I guess, after all what happened).<br />This book is highly recommended. For who value friendship. For who doesn't believe in friendship. For handsome guy like Jack Folley who finally let go the only girl he really love and care about, just because he took it for granted and couldn't control himself from looking around. For big girls out there with big heart that sometimes doubt about whether being virgin is still up to date.<br /><br />Btw, this book already filmed, Chris O' Donnel as the handsome Jack. I haven't watch the movie (already tried to find the movie, but couldn' t find it! So if you happened to know, let me know where to find it in Jakarta)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_686742545">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686742545" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15939692-trish-at-between-my-lines" class="left imgcol" title="Trish at Between My Lines"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1436089062p2/15939692.jpg" alt="Trish at Between My Lines" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/686742545?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15939692-trish-at-between-my-lines" class="user" title="Trish at Between My Lines">Trish at Between My Lines</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/41977.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099498599" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer686742545">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3322722752677270307">Do you have a favourite pair of old jeans? Worn to death, washed to that perfect comfortable feel, not the latest edgy trendy cut and colour but still a firm favourite. They are a perfect fit and make you feel good. Ones you pull out and wear time after time? Circle of Friends is the book equivalent of those jeans for me. Around forever, radiating warmth, full of humour and with a gossipy, uplifting plot. Yes, it’s another of my comfort books.<br /><br />Big hearted, generous Benny is the main character. Fr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3322722752677270307">Do you have a favourite pair of old jeans? Worn to death, washed to that perfect comfortable feel, not the latest edgy trendy cut and colour but still a firm favourite. They are a perfect fit and make you feel good. Ones you pull out and wear time after time? Circle of Friends is the book equivalent of those jeans for me. Around forever, radiating warmth, full of humour and with a gossipy, uplifting plot. Yes, it’s another of my comfort books.<br /><br />Big hearted, generous Benny is the main character. From a child, she has been heavy or as others non too delicately put it – a lump of a child, a heifer, large and square. On her 10th birthday, she is expecting a princess party dress to transform her but instead she gets a ‘sturdy, hard wearing outfit’ that her parents have finished off with matching shoes and handbag. Benny never tells them that this broke her heart instead she smiles through the pain and pretends excitement.<br /><br />This book focuses on Benny and best friend Eve leaving their small, country town to attend college in Dublin. Benny is vibrant, charismatic, funny and tender hearted. In Dublin, Benny and Eve find new battles to be fought, new friends to be made as they struggle to make their way in a rapidly changing Ireland. On their college menu is fun and frolics and a side order of backstabbing . The book is set in the 1950’s but despite the older setting, it’s very much a case that the problems faced by college going folks never changes. I faced the challenges in the 90s that Benny faced in the 50’s. I have no doubt the themes of friendship, loyalty, the difference in values and attitudes between parents and teenagers and issues over image are timeless and will continue to have meaning to new generations of readers.<br /><br />The first line draws me in <br /><br />“The kitchen was full of the smells of baking”<br /><br />This sounds like my home growing up where my mother was forever baking for all of us. It feels nostalgic and familiar. From that first line to the last line, I’m wrapped up in a rosy glow.<br /><br />The setting is so authentic, it catches an Ireland that is long gone but captured forever within the pages of Maeve Binchy’s books. A time when church had as much importance as the government. Communities where everyone knew you and all your business. If you coughed in your bedroom in privacy, the next day half the town would ask you how you chest infection was and remind you that lung problems run in your family and to make sure and look after it! A time when the younger generation were pulling the older generation kicking and screaming into the ‘racier’ 1950’s. Where a new jukebox in town caused uproar and new fashions such as miniskirts scandalised the more conservative.<br /><br />The book has a huge cast of great characters. All of them, full of life and fleshed out with remarkable detail. However, it’s Benny that won my heart. I was overweight when I was younger too and I can identify with the trouble this caused her. I had lost weight by the time I was college age but I know how it can eat away at you and destroy your confidence.<br /><br />“He drew her a little closer which was great except that she feared the place he had his hand on her back was just the part where the heavy-duty bra ended and there was a small roll of flesh. God suppose he held that bit of her – it would be like a lifebelt. How could she get him to move his hand up her back? How? These were things you needed to know in life, rather than what was set out in a syllabus for you.”<br /><br />This book makes me smile and I’m always rooting for Benny with her heart of gold. For a while she lives her fairy tale but unlike a fairy tale this one does not end happily ever after. Something I really appreciated about this book, it was realistic but still ended on an optimistic but not ridiculous note. Until they made a movie and changed the ending. Why? WHY? It made me so mad. <br /><br />Who should read this? <br /><br />Highly recommended to all who like character driven books, books with a strong sense of place with a heart warming and uplifting vibe. There is a reason Maeve Binchy sold more than 40 million copies of her books and if you have never read one, then this would be a good one to try</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3322722752677270307">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18354738932892781526">The best part about this book was the characters and how well they are portrayed.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer466779972">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4874896750294039047">Never before an author managed to keep me awake all night and hours beyond sun rise to finish their novel.<br />But Binchy did! And she did it twice.. Once about two years ago with The Glass Lake when I stayed with the book in my hand all night until 8 in the morning when I finally finished it AND yesterday as I stayed in bed from 11:30 till almost 7 in the morning with the little lamp guiding my eyes page after page as I impatiently yet gladly follow Binchy's plots..<br />No praise a humble reading like my</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4874896750294039047">Never before an author managed to keep me awake all night and hours beyond sun rise to finish their novel.<br />But Binchy did! And she did it twice.. Once about two years ago with The Glass Lake when I stayed with the book in my hand all night until 8 in the morning when I finally finished it AND yesterday as I stayed in bed from 11:30 till almost 7 in the morning with the little lamp guiding my eyes page after page as I impatiently yet gladly follow Binchy's plots..<br />No praise a humble reading like myself would express my adoration for this author, her style, her depth and her realistic plots.<br />I simply adore her novels, connect with them, see reality in them and see them in reality.<br />Binchy takes you where your mind usually restrains itself either busy with life daily struggles or afraid to confront the harsh, complicated and complex reality of life.<br />I highly recommend this book to anyone who like, love or enjoy reading.. It will make you smile, hope and reflect..<br /><br />Done with the novel today Friday 30/11 at 11:47 (the last few pages were only left because by 7 I could really push myself any further after 27 hours of work)<br /><br />This review is written a couple of hours later at 14:39 :) </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4874896750294039047">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/133356-jan" class="left imgcol" title="Jan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1184766678p2/133356.jpg" alt="Jan" /></a>

      <a href="/user/show/133356-jan" class="user" title="Jan">Jan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1216209556">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7414239507552272930">I debated. four stars? five stars? I really liked this story about two girls who grow up in a small town and go to college in Dublin. Benny and Eve are fierce friends in a circle of friends who contain some who are not so true in the end. Is it a perfect book? Probably not. Did I enjoy it? Yes! The moral lines are subtle, but they are there. All the characters are fully drawn and the plot kept me reading - quite late on the night I finished it.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_152801822">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152801822" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4885067-lissa" class="left imgcol" title="Lissa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1407594070p2/4885067.jpg" alt="Lissa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/152801822?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 13, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4885067-lissa" class="user" title="Lissa">Lissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4885067-lissa?shelf=women-writers" class="actionLinkLite">women-writers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4885067-lissa?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4885067-lissa?shelf=20th-century" class="actionLinkLite">20th-century</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4885067-lissa?shelf=ireland" class="actionLinkLite">ireland</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4885067-lissa?shelf=library" class="actionLinkLite">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152801822">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10376283611588424613">I found a hard-cover version of <em>Circle of Friends</em> on my mother's bookcase one summer during high school. I read it through in less than two days, took it with me to college, and re-read it so many times over the net few years that the binding eventually gave out. I didn't replace it, figuring that I had every page memorized.<br /><br />The characters -- Benny Hogan, Eve Malone, Mother Francis, Peggy Pine, Mr. and Mrs. Hogan, Patsy, Sean Walsh, the Kennedys and Healys and Johnsons, Clodaugh, Mario and Fonsie</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10376283611588424613">I found a hard-cover version of <em>Circle of Friends</em> on my mother's bookcase one summer during high school. I read it through in less than two days, took it with me to college, and re-read it so many times over the net few years that the binding eventually gave out. I didn't replace it, figuring that I had every page memorized.<br /><br />The characters -- Benny Hogan, Eve Malone, Mother Francis, Peggy Pine, Mr. and Mrs. Hogan, Patsy, Sean Walsh, the Kennedys and Healys and Johnsons, Clodaugh, Mario and Fonsie, Kit Hegarty, Jack Foley and Aidan Lynch and Nan Mahon -- could be a person sitting opposite you on a bus, so real and full of personality and flaws and dreams are they. The situations they get themselves into, or find themselves lodged within, are simple ones, filled with drama and humour because of the deep care given to each human being involved. Even the villains aren't purely villainous; we see enough of the hopes and dreams and desires of Simon Westward, Sean Walsh, Nan Mahon, and Mrs. Healy that even their sins seem pardonable, their foibles human, their mistakes and lapses of judgment worthy of compassion.<br /><br />The story is magnificent. <a title="Maeve Binchy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3532.Maeve_Binchy">Maeve Binchy</a> spins Irish yarns of the commonplace and realistic with quiet dexterity, but this one hangs fully on the shoulders of the characters themselves. Abandoned orphans, desperately love only children, drunken and abusive parents, first steps away from home, stealing from an employer, courting one who can never love you, falling in love and being loved in return, infidelity, unplanned pregnancy, placing trust in the wrong person, accidental death, abandonment as an adult, loneliness, finding friends, realizing the dreams you've worked toward can never be true, or finding out that the things you've wished for might actually come to pass -- these are commonplace situations that individual people find themselves in all the time; we know our own stories, and those of our friends and relations, or the neighbors down the street whom we can't help but gossip about. And we care about this ending, this resolution, the steps that take place after the last page, because we care for these characters.<br /><br />Binchy creates friends for us in the pages of her novels, and in so doing, points the way to finding the friends we might never have had in the world outside it. What a gift.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10376283611588424613">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7286078843590144177">Another book not reviewed right after reading. Here's all I have:<br /><br />I knew that I wanted to write more on this lovely book, but that it would take some time and thought. Unfortunately, now, I have allowed too much time to pass, and can't remember much of what I wanted to write! *ack*<br /><br />What I do remember is that I found it fascinating to read this book while picturing the actress Minnie Driver as Benny. I loved having a face for her! And this book was truly enjoyable. In fact, if I had another copy on</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7286078843590144177">Another book not reviewed right after reading. Here's all I have:<br /><br />I knew that I wanted to write more on this lovely book, but that it would take some time and thought. Unfortunately, now, I have allowed too much time to pass, and can't remember much of what I wanted to write! *ack*<br /><br />What I do remember is that I found it fascinating to read this book while picturing the actress Minnie Driver as Benny. I loved having a face for her! And this book was truly enjoyable. In fact, if I had another copy on hand, it would go on a special pile of "books I'd like to re-read".<br /><br />I loved Mother Francis! I can't remember the last time I liked a character so much. It made me want to be Catholic :) I was so impressed with the things she said and did, and the way she helped mold lives. I think she must have been modelled after someone real the author knows/knew, or she couldn't have been quite so inspiring.<br /><br />The old cliché of "I laughed, I cried, a good time was had by all" was certainly true in this book. I did all of the above, and then some.<br /><br />Thoughts on the movie: very disappointing. 2 significant changes -- the movie starts when the girls go to university (not when they're 6 years old), and Mother Francis doesn't even exist in the movie. Don't waste your time on it. The book is the taste you want to leave in your mouth :)<br /><br />For an entertaining forum thread on British Trifle, spawned by reading this book, click <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.bookcrossing.com/forum/5/2443424/subj_-UK-friends:--a-question-about-trifle">here</a>.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_222449749">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222449749" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4665623-jenna-st-hilaire" class="left imgcol" title="Jenna St Hilaire"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1294032843p2/4665623.jpg" alt="Jenna St Hilaire" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/222449749?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 02, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4665623-jenna-st-hilaire" class="user" title="Jenna St Hilaire">Jenna St Hilaire</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/578234.Circle_of_Friends" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780340551332" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer222449749">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3128027833497724977">My friend Elizabeth bought this book for me, saying that Binchy’s writing is peaceful, relaxing and enjoyable to read. It is that. But I also had to stay up reading it till three A.M. in desperate suspense.<br /><br />It wasn’t due to relentless pacing or swift-moving prose. Binchy’s writing career apparently began before the modern outcry against things like the passive verb and the third person omniscient voice. Her brief sentences and snappy dialogue generally kept the scenes from dragging, though, and I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3128027833497724977">My friend Elizabeth bought this book for me, saying that Binchy’s writing is peaceful, relaxing and enjoyable to read. It is that. But I also had to stay up reading it till three A.M. in desperate suspense.<br /><br />It wasn’t due to relentless pacing or swift-moving prose. Binchy’s writing career apparently began before the modern outcry against things like the passive verb and the third person omniscient voice. Her brief sentences and snappy dialogue generally kept the scenes from dragging, though, and I appreciated the easygoing nature of the tale.<br /><br />The characters delighted me. Taking the secondary cast for now, I particularly loved Mother Francis, Kit Hegarty, Heather, Aidan, Clodagh and Fonsie. I wound up liking Bill a good bit, too. He could be a touch tactless, but he seemed like a solid, good-natured guy. I rather wish we’d gotten more of him.<br /><br />Benny is an incredibly sympathetic protagonist. Most women know the feeling of having some physical flaw that we fear will turn men away, and when that flaw is noticeable enough to be pointed out again and again and again by everyone, it turns to torment. Benny’s humor and grace throughout make her lovable, someone I couldn't help wanting to be like.<br /><br />Eve is just as likable in her own way, primarily for her intense loyalty and sharp wit. She and Aidan share quite a few hilarious little dialogues; they and Clodagh and Fonsie provide much of the comedy in the story. And I’ve got to admit, I’ve made numerous re-reads of the scene where Eve confronts Nan, just for the satisfaction of her fierce defense of her friend and her home. Even though part of that defense was rather indefensible.<br /><br />The friendship between Eve and Benny carries the tale, beneath the numerous perspectives and the sweet but doomed romance. Yeah, I suppose that’s a little spoilerific. But that “sweet but doomed” bit is exactly why I stayed up till three—it was all so tender, and I really wanted it to work out, but I had myself braced for an explosion.<br /><br />I didn’t brace hard enough.<br /><br />The ending itself was beautiful and admirable and exactly what it should have been, if you’ll grant me the nitpicky writerly whim of disliking the last two lines as used together. I knew just why Binchy ended it the way she did, and the reasonable half of me cheers.<br /><br />Now, spoiler.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[The unreasonable half of me—the half that took three watches each through the movies <em>Sabrina</em> and <em>While You Were Sleeping</em> to accept that the setup romances were not the payoff romances—had a hard time with it. When a heroine falls in love with someone who turns out to be a rake, there’s admittedly no good way to resolve that. Rakes are notoriously difficult to reform; it’s a case of powerful addiction. But like any fool girl, I always hope that just once, the one in this or that story will change.<br /><br />And Jack Foley didn't strike me quite as a classic rake. At least, not at first. Binchy does an exceptional job at making the reader care about nearly every character, even the weak ones, and I really, really wanted to love the young charmer. Jack is handsome, lighthearted, very capable of being sweet, and falls in love with Benny for reals. He’s not messing around. Until, of course, he is. Benny can’t be there whenever he wants her, won’t go all the way in the back of the car, and along comes the temptress, and he’s toast.<br /><br />But Nan played Jack, too. He deserved nearly everything he got, but a part of me still hopes he learned his lesson and proved reformable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This book has been made into a movie—Minnie Driver’s first lead role, I believe, and with improvements enough to Jack’s character to pull off a classic happy ending. Both of which interest me in watching it; I am rather fond of happy endings and Minnie Driver. I like Chris O’Donnell, who plays Jack, too. On the other hand, the trailer makes it sound as if the movie’s theme is more “Catholic girls and sex” than friendship, which is unfortunate. Binchy does give an interesting and nuanced depiction of the former, but it’s a subservient theme and anyway, I’m not sure I trust the film industry to treat it quite so fairly.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3128027833497724977">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_386095257">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/386095257" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/125150-snail-in-danger-sid-nicolaides" class="left imgcol" title="Snail in Danger (Sid) Nicolaides"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1304526668p2/125150.jpg" alt="Snail in Danger (Sid) Nicolaides" /></a>

      <a href="/user/show/125150-snail-in-danger-sid-nicolaides" class="user" title="Snail in Danger (Sid) Nicolaides">Snail in Danger (Sid) Nicolaides</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer386095257">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2961441506401851756">More like 2.5. I was feeling in the mood to read something cozy and glurge-y that I didn't need to use much brainpower to read. So something made me think of this. I suspect it was seeing the third of the Dark Knight Batman films, and being reminded of the previous series of Batman films. Yes, there <em>is</em> a connection — Batman Forever featured Chris O'Donnell as Robin, and in the movie version of this book (which came out in the same year) he played the male lead. (For a while he was a major teen h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2961441506401851756">More like 2.5. I was feeling in the mood to read something cozy and glurge-y that I didn't need to use much brainpower to read. So something made me think of this. I suspect it was seeing the third of the Dark Knight Batman films, and being reminded of the previous series of Batman films. Yes, there <em>is</em> a connection — Batman Forever featured Chris O'Donnell as Robin, and in the movie version of this book (which came out in the same year) he played the male lead. (For a while he was a major teen heartthrob.)<br /><br />I'm feeling a strong urge to rant about the changes that were made in the movie version but that's not really germane and is definitely spoilerish.<br /><br />This book made me a little bit uncomfortable to read. We're dealing with people growing up in a repressed Irish mostly Catholic environment, in the late 1950s. They are at least somewhat curious about sex, and have various interest levels in it, and the idea that premarital sex is a sin stuck to varying degrees. There were definitely parts when ... I don't know, consent as a concept was not something people philosophized about back then, I suppose. Despite the interesting characters, and despite the fact that there were no scenes where the use of force to compel sex was depicted, I felt like that boundary was being pushed or hinted at sometimes, and it made me uncomfortable.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/20044686-mary-kate" class="left imgcol" title="Mary Kate"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1423008459p2/20044686.jpg" alt="Mary Kate" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1290775851?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20044686-mary-kate" class="user" title="Mary Kate">Mary Kate</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/478120.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780385341738" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1290775851">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3594466192039356727">How very nice this book was!<br /><br />I'm not going to lie, when I saw the title, which is just nauseatingly cheesy, I did not think I would enjoy this book. I did not have high hopes. But it turned out to be such a pleasant and comforting read! These characters were lovely. I wish I could have Benny and Eve for friends. They seem wonderful.<br /><br />It was cleverly constructed, too, as a book. It is really rather long, nearly six hundred pages, but Binchy gets around that in two ways that I noticed. The first way</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3594466192039356727">How very nice this book was!<br /><br />I'm not going to lie, when I saw the title, which is just nauseatingly cheesy, I did not think I would enjoy this book. I did not have high hopes. But it turned out to be such a pleasant and comforting read! These characters were lovely. I wish I could have Benny and Eve for friends. They seem wonderful.<br /><br />It was cleverly constructed, too, as a book. It is really rather long, nearly six hundred pages, but Binchy gets around that in two ways that I noticed. The first way is that she introduces the characters as children. Letting us get to know them as kids allows those characters to wiggle into our hearts so that by the time we start to think, "Wow, this book is long," we are already too invested in them to care. The second clever thing is that within each chapter, the point of view switched frequently, allowing snippets of the several different stories to come together to make up one. <br /><br />This was just such a nice read. I can't say that enough. Usually I go in for the grit and the grime. I like my books dark and melodramatic. This book was a refreshing change. It was light and fluffy and a bit sentimental, but thoroughly and extremely entertaining nonetheless.<br /><br />I must also add that I am in love with Aidan and think he is a perfectly marvelous boy.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3594466192039356727">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4135744048954755460">This wasn't quite as good as "Tara Road" but you're sure to enjoy the interesting characters, especially the women, in this book. Benny and Eve are best friends who only become friends after Benny's mother asks her to invite the loner Eve to her 12th birthday party. We quickly move ahead to their first year away from home and the guys who become their boyfriends.<br /><br />Benny has her first love and has to deal with Jack's casual attitude toward women. Eve meets family that never cared if she existed.<br /><br />Alt</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4135744048954755460">This wasn't quite as good as "Tara Road" but you're sure to enjoy the interesting characters, especially the women, in this book. Benny and Eve are best friends who only become friends after Benny's mother asks her to invite the loner Eve to her 12th birthday party. We quickly move ahead to their first year away from home and the guys who become their boyfriends.<br /><br />Benny has her first love and has to deal with Jack's casual attitude toward women. Eve meets family that never cared if she existed.<br /><br />Although it's long, you'll enjoy the characters and the descriptions of life in the small town of Knockglen, Ireland, in 1957-58.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/4263280-shannon" class="user" title="Shannon">Shannon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/41977.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099498599" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer126285112">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11849957184740578941">While reading the book Circle of Friends, I happen to be very bored. The author went into too much depth of unnecessary subjects in the story. If the author hadn’t written as much as she did, then I might have a better appreciation for the book. However, the characters of the story were very depressing. Each and every character had a sad tragic story that followed them. From these tragic events, the people took the wrong path and or made the wrong choices. Which then made the book less interesti</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11849957184740578941">While reading the book Circle of Friends, I happen to be very bored. The author went into too much depth of unnecessary subjects in the story. If the author hadn’t written as much as she did, then I might have a better appreciation for the book. However, the characters of the story were very depressing. Each and every character had a sad tragic story that followed them. From these tragic events, the people took the wrong path and or made the wrong choices. Which then made the book less interesting and dry. <br /> In the beginning of the novel it goes into the relationship of two best friends. These two best friends are Benny and Eve. Benny has a very nice home life with parents that adore her. However Benny’s biggest problem in the beginning of the book is that she insecure about the way she looks. Eve grew up without her parents and lives in a convent her whole life. Eve’s problem is that her mother’s family wants nothing to do with her. <br /> The book then brings you to a different part of their lives in which they go to college. They both attend the same college together, University of Dublin. During their college years the book really takes off. They end up making this group of friends. In this group consist of love affairs and strong dislikes spread among them equally. Further into the novel tragic events happen, mostly to Eve and Benny at home. The book continuously goes on with secrets being unraveled and fixing their problems.<br /> This novel is long and dry. It is filled with unsatisfying characters and events. However if you like a long book filled with people dealing with problems. Then you might enjoy reading this one. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11849957184740578941">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/200758756?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 21, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3269646-amanda" class="user" title="Amanda">Amanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/41977.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099498599" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer200758756">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12662286807602451138">The joy of a Maeve Binchy novel - and Circle of Friends is no exception (in fact, is probably the best example of this) - is that you are utterly drawn into the lives of the characters. Binchy doesn't concern herself with a clever plot (here, the essence of the plot is that Benny and Eve head off to university in Dublin, and deals with the repercussions of what happens after this); rather, she wants to describe how her characters deal with life. There are never lengthy descriptions of place - di</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12662286807602451138">The joy of a Maeve Binchy novel - and Circle of Friends is no exception (in fact, is probably the best example of this) - is that you are utterly drawn into the lives of the characters. Binchy doesn't concern herself with a clever plot (here, the essence of the plot is that Benny and Eve head off to university in Dublin, and deals with the repercussions of what happens after this); rather, she wants to describe how her characters deal with life. There are never lengthy descriptions of place - dialogue is the manner in which Binchy drives her story.<br /><br />So, if Binchy had been unable to write dialogue, her novels would fail in a big way. Luckily, Binchy has an absolutely unerring ear for dialogue. Her characters talk so naturally, to the point that reading Circle of Friends feels like evesdropping on a conversation between real people.<br /><br />I particularly love Circle of Friends because it is a true coming of age story - two girls leaving a sleepy village and dealing with the bright lights of Dublin. Finding themselves; discovering new friends, but learning that their true and strong friendship is the best thing by far to help them survive the trials and tribulations of their new life.<br /><br />In addition to this, Benny has to try and extract herself from a constricting home life to find the freedom necessary to enjoy her new life. I really appreciated this aspect of the story, since I think many young people are familiar with the idea of parents not wanting to let go and still trying to exert control over their children. Benny's frustrations were written with a ring of truth.<br /><br />Maeve Binchy's novel are like a literary hug - warm and gentle, with a surprising wit and wisdom, and I think that Circle of Friends is the best of them. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12662286807602451138">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_46054059">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46054059" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2021711-jennifer-johnson" class="left imgcol" title="Jennifer Johnson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1380063238p2/2021711.jpg" alt="Jennifer Johnson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/46054059?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2021711-jennifer-johnson" class="user" title="Jennifer Johnson">Jennifer Johnson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/41977.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099498599" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46054059">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5743970016792335593">If you look at my bookshelf you'll notice that I really like Maeve Binchy, I've read a lot of her books. Her stories aren't wildy romantic, they aren't full of crazy events- in fact you could describe them as rather bland. For whatever reason though, I really enjoy reading them. It's a comforting read and on a cold day they make me feel warm on the inside, a little bit like chicken soup. (And since I really, really loathe the "Chicken Soup for the Soul" books, it's good that I have something tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5743970016792335593">If you look at my bookshelf you'll notice that I really like Maeve Binchy, I've read a lot of her books. Her stories aren't wildy romantic, they aren't full of crazy events- in fact you could describe them as rather bland. For whatever reason though, I really enjoy reading them. It's a comforting read and on a cold day they make me feel warm on the inside, a little bit like chicken soup. (And since I really, really loathe the "Chicken Soup for the Soul" books, it's good that I have something that can have the same effect on me.)<br /><br />Circle of Friends focuses on Benny and Anne, two best friends from a small town who go off to University and build their "circle of friends" to include the beautiful Nan and a group of others, including boys with the potential for romance. As it happens in a large group of mutual friends, people begin to pair off, and soon secrets and betrayals also become part of the circle. As the author demonstrates, there are times when individuals find themselves on the outside of the circle and times when they find themselves on the inside of the circle, but it's rare to be completely removed.<br /><br />I find the author writes in such a way that you really feel like you're able to imagine what the characters look like, you understand what motivates them. She provides enough back story, (that tends to be irrelevant at first, but always makes sense later on in the book), that you understand why your characters are they way they are. I do remember seeing the Minnie Driver/Chris O'Donnell movie version of the book, a long time ago, although I can't remember a single thing about the movie. (I've rented it and it's in the plan for today.) It's funny because I tend to remember a lot of what happens in Binchy's books- even more so than some of the more profound works of literature I've read. I'm giving this book a nice warm 7/10- perfect for a cold snowy day where are you do is curl up on the couch with a book to read. It begins slow, but builds like a fire and ends happy... like all books should.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5743970016792335593">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2874578999324304116">A good read, though I would not categorise it as un-put-downable as it has been listed somewhere.<br />Set in late 1950s it's the story of two girls, close friends growing up in a small town in Ireland. They start their college studies in Dublin, make new friends there and how the Dubliners impact their lives and how they find their feet back again.<br />Though a lot of things keep happening, the pace is not very fast but it keeps your interest till the end.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12179540621182355524">I love love love Binchy's novels Circle of Friends still being my favorite and I have read it numerous times.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText12179540621182355524">I love love love Binchy's novels Circle of Friends still being my favorite and I have read it numerous times. This is long story of a friendship and love and loss, there are no lapses or lulls. Benny, plain daughter of a merchant, and Eve, a proud orphan raised by nuns, are close friends growing up in the Irish village of Knockglen in the 1950s. When they go to university in Dublin together, their loyalty is tested by the addition of others to their circle, most notably the beautiful, mysterious Nan, an ambitious young woman determined to rise above her working-class origins. While Nan seizes opportunities, friendships and romances are kindled and damped; ugly duckling Benny becomes a swan, and true love almost conquers all. A great book</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12179540621182355524">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1177033837">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1177033837" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/34672471-rena-sherwood" class="left imgcol" title="Rena Sherwood"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442512051p2/34672471.jpg" alt="Rena Sherwood" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1177033837?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/34672471-rena-sherwood" class="user" title="Rena Sherwood">Rena Sherwood</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1424465.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099410867" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1177033837">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16757121211671905138">Circle of Friends (1990) is one of the late Irish writer Maeve Binchy’s best-loved novels. It’s one of her only works turned into a movie in 1995 (also called Circle of Friends.) It has many of the features and types of characters seen in Binchy are other works. It centers on the friendship between two very different girls, Benny and Eve.<br /><br />The novel is set in a fictional Irish suburb called Knockglen, where Bernadette, (“Benny”), daughter of the town’s tailor is already unofficially engaged to be</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16757121211671905138">Circle of Friends (1990) is one of the late Irish writer Maeve Binchy’s best-loved novels. It’s one of her only works turned into a movie in 1995 (also called Circle of Friends.) It has many of the features and types of characters seen in Binchy are other works. It centers on the friendship between two very different girls, Benny and Eve.<br /><br />The novel is set in a fictional Irish suburb called Knockglen, where Bernadette, (“Benny”), daughter of the town’s tailor is already unofficially engaged to be married to one of the workers in the tailor shop. It’s the daughter’s first day of University College Dublin and it not only changes her life forever, but it also changes the lives of all of her circle of friends.<br /><br />What the Book is About<br /><br />The novel is written mostly from the perspective of Benny. She grows up in a typical home and became overweight yet friendly. Her father suddenly dies, naming Benny as the sole heir of the family tailor shop. Benny has to quickly learn the business as well as help out in the lives of her friends. Benny is a likeable and believable protagonist as she isn’t too pretty, too rich or too smart. She learns about the business and about life at a speed easy for readers to keep up with.<br /><br />The main plot is supported by a few subplots. One subplot centers on the two girls’ mutual friend Kit Hagerty, whose son dies in a motorcycle accident. She runs a boarding house for university students. How she manages to cope is believable. Another subplot involves the misadventures of the glamorous student Nan Mahon. She comes from a dirt poor family and vows to marry into wealth. Both of these subplots are quite detailed but interweave well into the main plot without overwhelming it.<br /><br />Typical Binchy<br /><br />Although the book centers on the convoluted friendship between ugly Benny and her beautiful orphaned friend Eve, the book has many different characters that are well-fleshed out. These characters are familiar to any reader of Binchy’s works, which includes how “rich” poor people can be, a woman having an unplanned pregnancy, people who say “eejits” instead of “idiots” and men who aren’t quite as nice as they first seem to be.<br /><br />The only problem with Circle of Friends is that it is so much like other Binchy novel that it doesn’t really stand out on its own. The town of Knockglen can be interchanged with just about any other small Irish town in Binchy books. Some of the characters can also be interchanged with nearly identical characters in other Binchy books. It does contain fine writing and the pages keep on turning, but Binchy never deviated from her money-making formula. That’s a shame, because she was an excellent writer. If you only have time to read one Binchy book, you will enjoy Circle of Friends. Just do not read another Binchy book soon afterwards.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16757121211671905138">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I found it to be a slow starter, but this author knows how to weave her story deep within you, so you grow to know the characters so well that you feel like you know them.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9261881638157029920">I started reading Circle of Friends because it was lying round the house, and I had nothing else to read. I found it to be a slow starter, but this author knows how to weave her story deep within you, so you grow to know the characters so well that you feel like you know them. You become immersed in her lilting Irish world without noticing and you must know what happens to Benny and her friends.<br /><br />This is a slow burning gentle story that you get lost in, just don't expect it to be fast paced and twisting.</span>

  <div class="xhr_comment_body">

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10780232252586612512">I loved Circle of Friends precisely because it's a meandering tale, which is believable, absorbing and pleasantly whiles away a couple of hours. Don't read it if your preference is deep suspense, sex and violence. You will be disappointed!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/80347000?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 25, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1132408-meg---a-bookish-affair" class="user" title="Meg - A Bookish Affair">Meg - A Bookish Affair</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/41977.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099498599" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/1132408-meg---a-bookish-affair?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer80347000">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3709723597298636451">This has probably been my favorite Maeve Binchy book that I have read so far. One of the things that I like about Binchy is that she is very good at describing the characters and giving the back story of the characters.<br /><br />Circle of Friends tell the story of Benny and Eve, friends who grow up in a small town in Ireland. They go off to university in Dublin where their circle of friends grows and their lives change greatly. This is a story of friends and the changes we go through as we grow up. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/267219905?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 30, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6147800-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/41977.Circle_of_Friends" title="Paperback 9780099498599" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6147800-kim?shelf=big-book-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">big-book-challenge</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer267219905'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer267219905">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10872775710766693937">At first it was a little hard for me to get into this novel. I have never before read a story that was taking place in Ireland and therefore some of the lingo and ways of the time period had me a bit lost.<br />However, once I was in, I was hooked. I rooted for Benny most of the nocel and cursed the characters of Nana Mahona nd Sean Walsh<br />I wanted Benny to be with Jack, bit in the end I think it was the path "the wise woman" would have chosen and am not disappointed. A very good novel</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_251926').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_251926').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script>
</li>
</ul>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3532.Maeve_Binchy">About Maeve Binchy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3532.Maeve_Binchy"><img alt="3532" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1206566579p2/3532.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer3556227738294643953">Maeve Binchy was born on 28 May 1940 in Dalkey, County Dublin, Ireland, the eldest child of four. Her parents were very positive and provided her with a happy childhood. Although she described herself as an overweight child, her parents' attitude gave her the confidence to accept herself for who she was.<br /><br />She studied at University College Dublin and was a teacher for a while. She also loved travelin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3556227738294643953">Maeve Binchy was born on 28 May 1940 in Dalkey, County Dublin, Ireland, the eldest child of four. Her parents were very positive and provided her with a happy childhood. Although she described herself as an overweight child, her parents' attitude gave her the confidence to accept herself for who she was.<br /><br />She studied at University College Dublin and was a teacher for a while. She also loved traveling, and this was how she found her niche as a writer. She liked going to different places, such as a Kibbutz in Israel, and she worked in a camp in the United States. While she was away, she sent letters home to her parents. They were so impressed with these chatty letters from all over the world that they decided to send them to a newspaper. After these letters were published, Maeve left teaching and became a journalist. <br /><br />Maeve married <a title=" Gordon Snell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/175193._Gordon_Snell"> Gordon Snell</a>, writer and editor of children's books. When they were struggling financially, <em>Light a Penny Candle</em> was published, which made her an overnight success. Many of her books, such as <em>Echoes</em>, are set in the past in Ireland. Some of her later novels, such as <em>Evening Class</em>, take place in more modern times. Her books often deal with people who are young, fall in love, have families, and deal with relationship or family problems. The main characters are people whom readers can empathise with. <br /><br />She passed away on 30 July 2012, at the age of 72.<br /><br />Her cousin <a title=" Dan Binchy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/249472._Dan_Binchy"> Dan Binchy</a> is also a published writer, as is her nephew <a title=" Chris Binchy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/380602._Chris_Binchy"> Chris Binchy</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3556227738294643953">...more</a>

    </div>
